asked the Minister of Power and Energy:

(a) Will he inform this House of the Grama NiladhariDivisions with their respective DivisionalSecretaries Divisions, which come under thejurisdiction of the Consumer Services Centre of theCeylon Electricity Board of Beliatta?

(b) Will he state separately the number of transformersstationed in the area of this Consumer ServicesCentre as at June 01, 2006 and where they arestationed?

(c) Will he state in this House separately —

(i) the number of consumers who have obtainedconnections from each suchtransformer forpurposes such as religious, domestic, commercialetc.;

(ii) the number of transformers in the entire areacovered with three phase electricity lines; and

(iii) will he state, with reference to the electricaltransformer concerned, the areas identified bythe Ceylon Electricity Board as those which donot get the proper voltage in the aboveConsumer Services centre area?

(d) If not, why?

asked the Prime Minister, Minister of Internal Administrationand Deputy Minister of Defence:

(a) Will he inform this House —

(i) when was the Hilton Hotel constructed;

(ii) the names of the shareholders along with theirpercentage of shares held at the inception;

(iii) the names of the present shareholders;

(iv) the anticipated cost outlay at the beginning andthe final cost;

(v) the amount paid by the Government againstoutstanding; and

(vi) the amount due and to whom?

(b) Will he state the net asset value as at today of theHilton Hotel to the owing shareholders?

(c) If not, why?

asked the Minister of Public Administration and HomeAffairs :

(a) Will he inform this House,—

(i) the number of pensioners in Sri Lanka perdistrict basis;

(ii) the total cost of pensions to-date per year basisfor the last five years:

(iii) the aforesaid pensions against total revenue ofthe Government and against Gross DomesticProduct (GDP); and

(iv) the envisaged cost for pensioners for the nextfive years per year basis?

(b) Will he state,—

(i) the increases given to the pensioners for the last10 years to-date;

(ii) whether they were implemented; and

(iii) if so, when?

(c) If not, why?

(b) Will she state —

(i) the action taken to curb this crime; and(ii) if not, the action taken against the “Daily News”newspaper for irresponsible reporting?(c) Will she submit to this House —

(d) If not, why?

asked the Minister of Trade, Commerce, Consumer Affairsand Marketing Development and Minister of Highways:

(a) Will he inform this House whether the companynamed Kumagai Gumi Ltd, which is engaged inthe construction of the super high way fromKurundugahahethekma to Matara under theMinistry of Highways, has employed foreignworkers?

(b) If so, will he submit to this House, separately,—

(i) the name of such workers and their countries ofdomicile;

(ii) their professional qualifications;

(iii) the salaries including all allowances paid tothem monthly; and,

(iv) the facilities and privileges afforded to them?(c) Will he state,—

(i) whether all the said foreign workers hold validvisas;

(ii) whether any of them are engaged in work underthe said company on tourist visas; and,(iii) if so, their names and the countries of domicile?

(d) If not, why?

asked the Minister of Disaster Management and HumanRights :(a) Will he inform this House —(i) the number of houses destroyed in the Tsunamiin the Habaraduwa, Galle, Hikkaduwa,Ambalangoda and Balapitiya DivisionalSecretariat Divisions in the Galle District;(ii) out of the persons who were displaced by theTsunami the number of persons who have beenprovided with houses by now;(iii) whether those houses have been built by theNon-Governmental Organizations or by theGovernment; and(iv) the number of people who are still living intemporary houses in the aforesaid DivisionalSecretaries Divisions?(b) Will he state,—(i) out of the persons who were displaced asmentioned above, the number of person whohave not been provided with houses they need:and(ii) the period of time which will be necessary forproviding house to the aforesadi persons?

(d) If not, why?

[1.33 p. m.]

ªÇæ ÇÉêÏà Í¨ù ÄÍºå(ºÇ®ÚºÈÐ ¼¨¹Æ Ä¯ÉºÆ)(The Hon. Rauff Hakeem)

Bismillahir Rahmanir Raheem

Hon. Deputy Speaker, may I take this opportunity towish you and all the Members of the House a Happy NewYear. With that sentiment, the Sri Lanka Muslim Congresswishes to make its contribution in this Debate to extendthe state of Emergency once again. At the very outset, Iwould like to remind the Government that we proposeto support this resolution on the condition that theextension of the state of Emergency should be used strictlyfor the purposes for which it is being promulgated.

We have seen some controversial incidents in the recentpast relating to issues of media freedom, issues pertainingto violation of human rights of the common people of thiscountry and we hope the Government would be quitesensitive to the concerns of parties like ours which havesome serious reservations about the way in which theEmergency Regulations are being used to protect thesovereignty of this country. It is very apt, I believe Mr.Deputy Speaker.

Today I read a news item on page four of the “DailyMirror” newspaper. This news item is attributed to the Hon.Minister of Cultural Affairs and National Heritage, the Hon.Mahinda Yapa Abeywardena. He says, “2007 named‘National year of drama.’ He, of course, is referring to theupliftment of the artistes and their famed skills in thiscountry. But when you go to look at variouspronouncements that are being made from the Governmentside we sure will be in for a year of drama. We have seenthe untold difficulties that the common man is undergoingtoday. If both the husband and wife are working and theyare to take the public transport, both of them do not traveltogether these days. They want at least one breadwinneralive if something unforeseen happens. For those peoplein the Northern and Eastern Provinces and many other partsof the bordering districts travelling to Colombo and other

ÀåÚÈèï¾àºëÉ127128

[ªÇæ ÇÉêÏà Í¨ù ÄÍºå]areas are fraught with so much of difficulties. They willhave to alight from the bus several times over, open theirbags and subject themselves to examinations and theirjourney is delayed by several hours.

We see many traffic snarls in the city and valuable manhours are being lost. The tourism industry is in thedoldrums. The economy is facing a very bleak prospectin this year. This being the case, we certainly are in fora “National year of drama.” In this midst, parties like oursare also living in hope of the impossible happening. Thehappenings in the APRC and the All Party Conference willbe a meaningless exercise, if we are to prusue a resolutionto the national ethnic problem in the manner in which weare proceeding these days. We would appeal to theGovernment to exercise restraint.

It is good for the Government to bear in mind that inthe Eastern Province LTTE never won battles andestablished camps. It has always been when the GovernmentForces themselves vacated the camps LTTE came andestablished themselves in those camps. I represent theEastern Province and I have been in this House from 1994.It was the previous administration after the failed talks in1995 that voluntarily vacated many camps in the EasternProvince. It was in that backdrop that the LTTE was ableto establish some control over those areas where they hadbrought large sections of people under their control. Ofcourse, there were some far-flung areas which had someLTTE activity. But very many places that came under thecontrol of the LTTE was not due to the fighting skills ofthe LTTE to capture territory, particularly in the EasternProvince. In the North, it is a different kettle of fish. Theywon territory by engaging in conventional war. But in theEastern Province no such massive military operations wereconducted in order to win over Government Security Forcecamps. They were all abandoned by the Governmentvoluntarily in order to capture territory and to strengthenthe forces in the Northern Province. Therefore, recapturingthe East even if the impossible happens is not going tobe a surprise. But in the meantime, there are otherresponsibilities cast on the Government.

It is my bounden duty to bring it to the notice of theGovernment. This is why we say that this year, 2007 isgoing to be a national year of drama. Mr. Deputy Speaker,it is very pertinent to read the article published in themiddle page of the “Daily Mirror” newspaper of todaytitled “Rajapaksa bent on dictated peace” . This article iswritten by none other than a former head of the IndianIntelligence Service, Research and Analysis Wing, Mr. B.Raman. There is a very pertinent statement he makes here.

It states, I quote :“The fighters of the anti-LTTE faction headed byKaruna are now openly assisting the Army in itsiperations in the Eastern Province. No effort is made

any longer to conceal the presence and key role ofthe followers of Karuna in the military operationsin the Eastern Province.”

This of course, is purely a military matter regarding whichthe SLMC does not want to make a comment. But, if itimpinges on the security of the innocent civilian populationthen it is our duty to bring it to the notice of theGovernment. We see today TMVP offices being openedvery adjacent to security forces camps. Several of thosecamps have come up in the Eastern Province. It is not amatter of secrecy any more as Mr. Raman states in thisreport. The Government is not endeavouring to distanceitself. Of course, there are other preposterous and may besubstantiated allegations that are being brought aboutregarding child conscription and assistance by Sri Lankanarmed forces for that activity which again is a matter leftfor the Government to defend. But, then, in many areasthe law and order machinery of the Government is turninga blind eye to the activities of the Karuna group when itaffects the civilians in many areas where they haveestablished their camps. The Muslim community remaineda very neutral party in the entire phase of hostilities notonly now but even in the past. There have been attemptsto drag the Muslim community into the hostilities. Theyhave suffered immensely for being neutral. They have beenmassacred in large numbers in villages. But, yet they neverdid anything overtly to deter the struggle of any communityin this country. Sinhalese civilians have been affected.Like the Muslims in many areas in the Eastern Province,Sinhalese have suffered. As a matter of fact, in theBatticaloa District alone 23 Muslim villages have had tobe vacated because of LTTE activities. The LTTE chasedaway Muslims from 23 villages and more than 90 per centof those Muslim villagers from these 23 hamlets came andlived in a very small area adjacent to Kattankudi, a verylarge Muslim village in the Batticaloa District. Perhaps,it is a village with the highest concentration in the entireSouth Asian region. Within an area of one and a half squareKilometres more than 65,000 people are living and, here,some recent incidents have been a matter of concern andit is my bounden duty to bring it to the notice of theGovernment that the activities of the Karuna faction in thatarea is giving room for serious apprehension among theMuslims. Recently, there was an attempt to settle refugeeswho came from Vakarai in an area called Karbala belongingto Muslims between Palamunai and Kattankudi. It is verynext to a Tamil village called Arayampathi. There is a STFcamp situated there. Just next to the STF camp is a Karunacamp. These cadres from this camp have attempted to burya dead body in a land belonging to the Muslims wherean altercation took place, From then onwards they havevery actively got involved in creating unnecessarycommunal tension in the area. Poor Muslims who went toengage in business in Arayampathi were chased away. Theywere asked to close their shops and go back to theirvillages. Even during the time when the LTTE was incontrol of this area, similar thing happened inKaluwanchikudi. During the time of the UNP Government

2007 °¾ÉåÖ 09129130

when Muslims went to do business in the Kaluwanchikudimarket, they were chased away forcibly. There was anattempt to forcibly grab land. The Mulsim community, asyou know, is not an armed community. They depend onthe Government law and order machinery for theirprotection. What is happening today is that in order to getthe assistance of the Karuna faction to fight the war againstthe LTTE some of their actions are being condoned. Theycan very flagrantly violate any law of this country and getaway with it. Complaints made against them are not beinginquired into by the local police and this is a very serioussituation. I appeal to the Government to look into thecomplaints that are being made against the cadres of theKaruna faction. We also appeal to the leaders of the Karunafaction not to encourage the activities of some of thesemiscreants within their ranks. We have nothing againstanyone in this regard except to Say that the Police beresponsible to maintain law and order. The police cannotcast is responsibility on others and certainly this mischief,if it is allowed to go any further, is going to result in veryserious repercussions for law and order in the entire area.
